<span id="freeTextContainer14423665554953171517">Deep in the heart of the darkest region of the Congo, near the legendary ruins of the Lost City of Zinj, an eight-person field expedition dies mysteriously and brutally in a matter of minutes.<br /><br />Ten thousand miles away, at the Houston-based Earth Resources Technology Services, Inc., supervisor Karen Ross—watches a gruesome video transmission of that ill-fated team: a camp des</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14423665554953171517">Deep in the heart of the darkest region of the Congo, near the legendary ruins of the Lost City of Zinj, an eight-person field expedition dies mysteriously and brutally in a matter of minutes.<br /><br />Ten thousand miles away, at the Houston-based Earth Resources Technology Services, Inc., supervisor Karen Ross—watches a gruesome video transmission of that ill-fated team: a camp destroyed, tents crushed and torn, equipment scattered in the mud alongside bodies…and the grainy, moving image of a dark, blurred shape.<br /><br />In San Francisco, primatologist Peter Elliot works with Amy, an extraordinary gorilla with a 620 “sign” vocabulary and a fondness for finger painting. Her recent drawing matches, with stunning accuracy, the frayed, brittle pages of a Portuguese print dating back to 1642…a drawing of the ancient lost city.<br /><br />Immediately, a new expedition is sent into the Congo, descending into a secret world where the only way out may be through the grisliest death…</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_285969330">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/285969330" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday" class="left imgcol" title="mark monday"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1446402303p2/131922.jpg" alt="mark monday" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/285969330?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 29, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday" class="user" title="mark monday">mark monday</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6326950-congo" title="Paperback 9780061782558" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=blood-and-danger" class="actionLinkLite">blood-and-danger</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer285969330">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7953946496777733078">i'm having a little trouble with myself right now. i just gave this one 4 stars and Inner-Snob Mark is getting very twitchy, almost trigger-happy, ready to take control of my favorite hand and bump this one down to 3 stars. never fear, i have a tight rein on Inner-Snob Mark and have carefully compartmentalized him away tonight. but he does have a few good points. my God, i gave the timeless classic The Last Unicorn 3 stars. i gave Room - which wrecked me emotionally and had me crying like someon</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7953946496777733078">i'm having a little trouble with myself right now. i just gave this one 4 stars and Inner-Snob Mark is getting very twitchy, almost trigger-happy, ready to take control of my favorite hand and bump this one down to 3 stars. never fear, i have a tight rein on Inner-Snob Mark and have carefully compartmentalized him away tonight. but he does have a few good points. my God, i gave the timeless classic The Last Unicorn 3 stars. i gave Room - which wrecked me emotionally and had me crying like someone died - the same 4 stars. and Congo gets only 1 star less than either Picnic at Hanging Rock or The Thin Red Line - two books that i think are perfect from beginning to end. eh, so fucken what. stars are stupid, right?<br /><br />okay, so that's the disclaimer. it will probably be longer than the actual review.<br /><br />i LOVED this book. it was one of those immersive experiences, one that i dived into and stayed deep. Crichton is not known for having an interesting writing style, but his prose is clean &amp; straightforward &amp; dry without being off-puttingly clinical. <em>ack, Inner-Snob Mark just had a spasm when i used the words "Crichton" and "prose" in the same sentence.</em> no complaints whatsoever about the quality of writing. Congo is not corny and it is not emotionally manipulative and there aren't stupid lines where i start breathing loudly in frustration. what it does have is a superbly brisk narrative that does not falter despite the very dense level of information surrounding it. and that's another great thing: the very well-done infodumps. i'm going to sound a little schoolboy-ish here... but i learned so much! about the Congo, of course. but this being Crichton, i also learned a lot about apes and technology and corporate philosophies and tons of other interesting shite. the author makes sure all of his research is on the page and yet it didn't feel didactic and it didn't take away from the plot - if anything, it drew me in further.<br /><br />oh yeah, and it had one more awesome thing. in my GR friend Bill's words: <em>The big star in this story is Amy, a gorilla with a 620 sign vocabulary. After reading this, you will want a gorilla for a best friend.</em> ah, Amy... i know we would be fast friends!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7953946496777733078">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_399561065">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/399561065" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6880123-gandalf-the-red" class="left imgcol" title="Gandalf the Red"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451280734p2/6880123.jpg" alt="Gandalf the Red" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/399561065?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 29, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6880123-gandalf-the-red" class="user" title="Gandalf the Red">Gandalf the Red</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/10419175-congo" title="Mass Market Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of cryptid adventures and for those who love giant apes &amp; gorillas</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6880123-gandalf-the-red?shelf=cryptid-adventure" class="actionLinkLite">cryptid-adventure</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6880123-gandalf-the-red?shelf=cryptid-giant-apes" class="actionLinkLite">cryptid-giant-apes</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6880123-gandalf-the-red?shelf=tech-thriller" class="actionLinkLite">tech-thriller</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6880123-gandalf-the-red?shelf=i-own-paperback" class="actionLinkLite">i-own-paperback</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer399561065">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5749683915456372956"><pre> <img width="260" height="400" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388886r/749719._SX540_SY540_.jpg" /><br /></pre><br />First off, I've always gone bananas over books and movies that have giant apes &amp; big gorillas in them, going way back to when I was a kid, particularly with movie classics like, <a title="King Kong by Delos W. Lovelace" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13578816.King_Kong">King Kong</a> and <a title="Mighty Joe Young by Ernest B. Schoedsack" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12638044.Mighty_Joe_Young">Mighty Joe Young</a>, that were a blast for me and my brother to watch together.<br /><br />Reading books and watching movies about big apes helps me reconnect with those experiences I will always hold dear to me.<br /><br />I've been going ape over everything &amp; anything simian fiction-related ever since. <br /><br />When I first saw the</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5749683915456372956"><pre>  <img width="260" height="400" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388886r/749719._SX540_SY540_.jpg" /><br /></pre><br />First off, I've always gone bananas over books and movies that have giant apes &amp; big gorillas in them, going way back to when I was a kid, particularly with movie classics like, <a title="King Kong by Delos W. Lovelace" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13578816.King_Kong">King Kong</a> and <a title="Mighty Joe Young by Ernest B. Schoedsack" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12638044.Mighty_Joe_Young">Mighty Joe Young</a>, that were a blast for me and my brother to watch together.<br /><br />Reading books and watching movies about big apes helps me reconnect with those experiences I will always hold dear to me.<br /><br />I've been going ape over everything &amp; anything simian fiction-related ever since. <br /><br />When I first saw the preview for the movie, <a title="Congo by Michael Crichton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1014377.Congo">Congo</a>, it was a no-brainer that I would be seeing it as soon as it came out. <br /><br />Anyone who may have seen the original advertisements for the movie, may remember that the 1st preview centered on character, <strong>Charles Travis</strong>, played by fan-favorite actor, <a title="Bruce Campbell" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1362939.Bruce_Campbell">Bruce Campbell</a>. <strong>*</strong>Ever since I first saw <a title="Evil Dead Companion by Bill Warren" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6072791.Evil_Dead_Companion">Evil Dead</a>, starring <a title="Bruce Campbell" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1362939.Bruce_Campbell">Bruce Campbell</a> as <strong>Ash</strong>, I followed every single film he did. But, if you saw <a title="Making of Congo by Jody Duncan" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1323174.Making_of_Congo">Congo</a>, then you'll know that he was only in the film for about 5 minutes or less! <br /><br /><img width="384" height="226" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407892167i/10776131._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br />I rushed out to see the 1st showing on the 1st day of the film release with my best friend, Doug, at the time. <br /><br /><strong>Before I read the book</strong>. <br /><br /><img width="384" height="216" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388886r/749721._SX540_SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br />I knew it was gonna have a <a title="Jurassic Park by Michael Crichton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7653482.Jurassic_Park">Jurassic Park</a> sorta cheeziness to it but I was looking forward to that and otherwise not really knowing what else to expect. The acting was a mixed bag of fine performances like <a title="Laura Linney" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/571279.Laura_Linney">Laura Linney</a> and <strong>Dylan Walsh</strong>, along with some of the worst acting since the very dawn of time. <a title="Tim Curry" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/258912.Tim_Curry">Tim Curry</a>, an actor I've loved since watching his iconic legendary performance as <strong>Dr. Frank-N-Furter</strong> in <a title="The Official Rocky Horror Picture Show Movie Novel by Richard J. Anobile" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3199596.The_Official_Rocky_Horror_Picture_Show_Movie_Novel">The Rocky Horror Picture Show</a> many many times, was just God-awful! As <strong>Herkermer Homolka</strong>, his Russian accent defies logic as to why they would even keep the cameras rolling after his first line, Which, to me, sounded like he got his tongue stuck in his throat. <br /><br /><img width="400" height="280" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388886r/749722._SX540_SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br />Though, by this point, I wouldn't trade him in for the world though his is the worst accent I've ever heard! <strong>*</strong>Now that I think about it, the way over-the-top French accent by <a title="Julia Ormond" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3867723.Julia_Ormond">Julia Ormond</a> in <a title="Mad Men the Illustrated World by Dyna Moe" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8456710.Mad_Men_the_Illustrated_World">Mad Men</a> is definitely up there for debate! ~ I'm guessing that the <a title="Mad Men the Illustrated World by Dyna Moe" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8456710.Mad_Men_the_Illustrated_World">Mad Men</a> producers must've got confused thinking she was French actress, <a title="Juliette Binoche" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/730909.Juliette_Binoche">Juliette Binoche</a>, when they brought her on, since they look dead-on identical!:<br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://0d.img.v4.skyrock.net/2749/19572749/pics/2999350835_1_3_NMfXs8Cv.jpg" target="_blank">http://0d.img.v4.skyrock.net/2749/195...</a><br /><br />Back to Congo. As my buddy Doug and I watched the film we kept sinking lower and lower and lower into our seats until we were, seriously, nearly sitting on the ground. Throughout all the impossibilities that could <em>only</em> happen in an 80's movie, we burst out laughing in places where we weren't supposed to dozens of times! (much to the hatred of the rest of the audience, I'm sure). By the end of the movie, as we were walking out, I said in my best Amy voice - the pet gorilla who had the female equivalent of a <a title="Stephen Hawking" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1401.Stephen_Hawking">Stephen Hawking</a>-like computer voicebox -<strong>
  <em> "Bad movie, Amy, Bad movie."</em>
</strong> Yeah...we were little shi†s then just like most guys that age, I guess.<br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388886r/749723._SX540_SY540_.png" /><br /><br />Just so you know, I've watched the film a few times since and it gets better every time. It's a real hoot! and now I think I love it!<br /><br />But, back to the book. <br /><br />In case it surprises anybody, I don't think <a title="Michael Crichton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton">Michael Crichton</a> wrote this one <strong>just so</strong> it would turn out to be a mega-million-buck movie. <br /><br />And though it's a tech-thriller, it's also a throwback to the pulp adventure-style books going on for over a century now. Most notably, <a title="King Solomon's Mines by H. Rider Haggard" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/751789.King_Solomon_s_Mines">King Solomon's Mines</a>:<br /><pre>  <img width="297" height="460" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388886r/749724._SX540_SY540_.jpg" /></pre><br />The difference? It's been updated, everything moves faster, there's better equipment, and <em>everybody's</em> more sarcastic and cynical than ever before. No duh really!?<br /><br />I really enjoyed this novel. I'm pretty sure everybody has an idea what it's about so why go into it. <br /><br />It was a good book. <br /><br />However...<br /><br />Since most of the covers, including the movie poster and dvd, have a GORILLA on it, you would expect there to be some damn gorillas IN IT. <br /><br />I kept asking:<br /><pre>  <img width="300" height="300" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407546511i/10737496.jpg" /></pre><br />...a common question I ask whenever I expect to see more of something, or, when there's an element sorely missing throughout what I'm reading!<br /><br />Here's one where you would want <a title="Michael Crichton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton">Michael Crichton</a> to use his time machine from <a title="Timeline by Michael Crichton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13573415.Timeline">Timeline</a> so he could fast forward to the future and take notes of the formula that worked so well in books he wrote later and were more successful. <a title="Jurassic Park by Michael Crichton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7653482.Jurassic_Park">Jurassic Park</a> had a great abundance of dinosaurs in it. Too bad he couldn't have done the same and put his theory to work here!<br /><br />It is a well written, nicely plotted book, with good characters, a great premise, action-packed, and mostly a lot of fun. <br /><br />It was just missing one thing for me: <strong>MORE FREAKING GORILLAS!</strong><br /><br /><img width="400" height="229" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388886r/749727._SX540_SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>*</strong> This is one of those rare books that has many great artwork covered editions. I hope you pick a good one. Buying the bland books allows the publisher to think it's ok to skip the art department, leaving us with a world of mediocre book covers to choose from. So you know, many of the cheapest editions have some very nice covers.<br /><br /><img width="400" height="280" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388886r/749728._SX540_SY540_.jpg" /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5749683915456372956">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_136577076">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/136577076" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1500718-ryan" class="left imgcol" title="Ryan"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1238846167p2/1500718.jpg" alt="Ryan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/136577076?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 28, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1500718-ryan" class="user" title="Ryan">Ryan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7672.Congo" title="Paperback 9780060541835" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer136577076">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14519768147050045816">Michael Crichton's work should be considered the epitome of geek literature (AKA science fiction, genre fiction, or speculative fiction), but was somehow embraced by the mainstream -- so much so that even if the academic crowd doesn't take him very seriously, Crichton still addressed Congress. Genre fiction is such a dismissive term, so Crichton was given his own genre: it's not geek; it's a "techno thriller."<br /><br /><em>Congo</em>, published in 1980, has all of Crichton's geekiest motifs, including a heroine wh</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14519768147050045816">Michael Crichton's work should be considered the epitome of geek literature (AKA science fiction, genre fiction, or speculative fiction), but was somehow embraced by the mainstream -- so much so that even if the academic crowd doesn't take him very seriously, Crichton still addressed Congress. Genre fiction is such a dismissive term, so Crichton was given his own genre: it's not geek; it's a "techno thriller."<br /><br /><em>Congo</em>, published in 1980, has all of Crichton's geekiest motifs, including a heroine whose tragic flaw is revealed on -- get this -- a computer printout. It's a pretty obvious way of characterizing one's hero, but it works. And give him credit, unlike in <em>The Andromeda Strain</em>, Crichton actually has characters with personalities and internal conflicts in <em>Congo</em>. Clearly, this is an author on the rise.<br /><br /><em>Congo</em> works in the same way that <em>Sphere</em> (1987) and <em>Jurassic Park</em> (1990) -- my favorite Crichton titles -- work. A team of scientists is sent on a dangerous mission that will require technical expertise, ingenuity, and a conflict between ambition and responsibility. I love that Crichton takes the ideal neutrality and benefits of science and juxtaposes them with the realities of funding, application, and career ambition. These three works also serve to map out what I believe is Crichton approaching and reaching the peak of his writing. My only wish is that I would have read <em>Congo</em> first, rather than third.<br /><br /><em>Congo</em> was not only published first in this thematic and structural trilogy, but it is clear that Crichton was consciously improving his writing in each of these novels. In <em>Congo</em>, he establishes the pattern by opening with a cool setting and a cool premise: jungle ruins and highly trained attack gorillas. Not bad.<br /><br />But he can do better.<br /><br /><em>Sphere</em> features the ocean floor and an alien technology that tests humanity's character. The characters are also more complex and engaging in <em>Sphere</em>, and I especially enjoyed Crichton's decision to make psychologist Norman Johnson the hero. <em>Sphere</em> is great, so everyone must have quite naturally expected that Crichton would begin the 1990s with his authorial decline.<br /><br />But then:<br /><br />In <em>Jurassic Park</em>, dinosaurs are brought back to life through cloning technology on a privately owned tropical island. Unbelievable! And let's not forget about Alan Grant and Ian Malcolm, arguably Crichton's most memorable academics, battling dinosaurs (don't gorillas just seem so "small potatoes" in comparison?) with nothing but their wits.<br /><br />So, for me, <em>Congo</em> is a very good work, but not a great one. However, perhaps this is only if we measure Crichton against himself.<br /><br />And it does not change the fact that <em>Congo</em>, <em>Sphere</em>, and <em>Jurassic Park</em> should be considered a required "trilogy" for all geeks -- sorry -- I meant "required reading for all 'techno thriller enthusiasts.'"</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14519768147050045816">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/2838753?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 08, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/169061-cpd" class="user" title="Cpd">Cpd</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7672.Congo" title="Paperback 9780060541835" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/169061-cpd?shelf=whativeread" class="actionLinkLite">whativeread</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer2838753">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14241785729034842495">I saw this on Chris' list and it triggered an old, funny memory. Now, I did read this book -- back in high school I went through a Michael Crichton phase and his books being as they are, I managed to read through his -- dare I say oevure? -- in a summer (don't recall which summer, tho')<br /><br />The odd memory that Chris triggered however, has to to do with the movie Congo. I had a good friend in high school, wonderful fella, still a great friend. About the time we were seniors, he started dating -- or as</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14241785729034842495">I saw this on Chris' list and it triggered an old, funny memory. Now, I did read this book -- back in high school I went through a Michael Crichton phase and his books being as they are, I managed to read through his -- dare I say oevure? -- in a summer (don't recall which summer, tho')<br /><br />The odd memory that Chris triggered however, has to to do with the movie Congo. I had a good friend in high school, wonderful fella, still a great friend. About the time we were seniors, he started dating -- or as the kids say, "going steady" with a...I think she was a sophomore at the time. The point is, Saturday nights I'd ask him:<br /><br />"What are you doing tonight?"<br />"We rented Congo."<br />"You rented that last week."<br />"..."<br /><br />And -- not lying -- we had the exchange roughly twice a month for the life of their relationship (about the length of the school year). Thus, when anyone in our circle of friends got lucky (for most of us a rare occurrence), we referred to it as "watching Congo." To use it in a sentence...<br /><br />"You watch Congo on Saturday?"<br />"You know how I roll."<br /><br />Etc., et.al.<br /><br />(granted, at the time, no one I knew said "how I roll," but it sounds better)<br /><br />In regards to the actual book, the only thing I remember is that I did not care much for it.<br /><br />~cpd<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14241785729034842495">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer15333902567865928635">Not bad in places...other times it's sort of a "puleez" book. Again Crichton has one that could have been better. The best I suppose I can say is..it wasn't as lame as the movie. So full of PC political rhetoric it seemed to me that any story got lost.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />************ Spoilers below Line ***********<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[The "Amy" character is just too sweet for words...I had to take insulin.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText15333902567865928635">Not bad in places...other times it's sort of a "puleez" book. Again Crichton has one that could have been better. The best I suppose I can say is..it wasn't as lame as the movie. So full of PC political rhetoric it seemed to me that any story got lost.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />************ Spoilers below Line ***********<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[The "Amy" character is just too sweet for words...I had to take insulin. I love animals, really I do, not setting up a joke here about eating meat. (Though I do eat meat). But I love animals and I know that Gorillas are not actually predators (Chimpanzees are,but that's another discussion)... BUT, the sign language using Gorilla and of course the secret of the "bad things" as Amy calls the aggressive gorillas (that they were made evil by evil humans) and the whole technology and advancement and the companies who build it are ALWAYS EVIL theme was for me just to much of a head slapper. Personally I enjoy having a flush toilet, using my computer, living in a dwelling that has heat in the winter and cooling in the summer, watching TV, listening to music whenever I like, having light at my fingertips when I want to read a book at night and all the other evil advances that have gotten us out of the jungle expanded our life spans to more than 30 or 40 years and so on. AND I believe it's possible to have those things without destroying nature and don't think all technological groups are out to destroy nature.<br /><br />The book is in other words at times silly...though not as silly as the movie with Amy's "talking backpack"... Oh come on please. <br /><br />I wonder if by now there's an entire tribe of Gorillas who "speak" sign language. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_20228256">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20228256" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1055362-michael-sorensen" class="left imgcol" title="Michael Sorensen"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442486716p2/1055362.jpg" alt="Michael Sorensen" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/20228256?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 15, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1055362-michael-sorensen" class="user" title="Michael Sorensen">Michael Sorensen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7672.Congo" title="Paperback 9780060541835" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer20228256'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer20228256">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9930328245934655323">Michael Crichton books all start off with this huge technological hook and are excellent at grabbing you by your ear and dragging you along, but somewhere along the way he fizzles. It's like he has this great idea, but can't figure out a way for his protagonists to create a successful ending. Andromeda Strain, the virus floats off into space--woo hoo. Sphere--the whole adventure was imaginary, woo hoo. Congo, earthquake wipes out all the lovely evidence and negates the whole adventure...boo hoo.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9930328245934655323">Michael Crichton books all start off with this huge technological hook and are excellent at grabbing you by your ear and dragging you along, but somewhere along the way he fizzles. It's like he has this great idea, but can't figure out a way for his protagonists to create a successful ending. Andromeda Strain, the virus floats off into space--woo hoo. Sphere--the whole adventure was imaginary, woo hoo. Congo, earthquake wipes out all the lovely evidence and negates the whole adventure...boo hoo. Ocassionally MC will get it right, but even with Juraissic Park, where the characters manage to escape with their lives--the ending is still ambivalent. Nothing was truly resolved. Quit being so wishy-washy MC and give us an ending we can sink our teeth into! </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9930328245934655323">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_779481896">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/779481896" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8187431-rade" class="left imgcol" title="Rade "><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1426096920p2/8187431.jpg" alt="Rade " /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/779481896?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 27, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8187431-rade" class="user" title="Rade ">Rade </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/96667.Congo" title="Hardcover 9780394513928" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8187431-rade?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer779481896">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11786693229966290777">what could have been a great adventure book turned out to be a barely mediocre writing effort on behalf of Crichton. Not that it is bad, it was just boring for me. Even the scenes where they were attacked were pretty boring. I know the author tends to dedicate a big portion of the book on background research but in this case I just did not care much for any of it. <br /><br />I felt the ending might be building up to something big but it got resolved in what seemed like to be a page or two. I felt let down.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11786693229966290777">what could have been a great adventure book turned out to be a barely mediocre writing effort on behalf of Crichton. Not that it is bad, it was just boring for me. Even the scenes where they were attacked were pretty boring. I know the author tends to dedicate a big portion of the book on background research but in this case I just did not care much for any of it. <br /><br />I felt the ending might be building up to something big but it got resolved in what seemed like to be a page or two. I felt let down. I felt the author was just writing things on the paper just so he can meet some deadline or something. That would explain uninteresting characters, lack of development of these so called characters and lack of me giving any shit about these characters. I did not like any of them besides Amy and Amy is a gorilla who uses sign language to communicate simple commands and or pleasures/displeasures. <br /><br />This was an alright book. It was in parts boring, in parts fun, in parts weird, and overall just an OK read. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11786693229966290777">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1498740000">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11777681081071192502">A science fiction novel by Michael Crichton.It is about an expedetion investigating the mysterious deaths of a previous expedition in the dense rain forest of Congo.it is a fairly realistic story (other than the trained killer apes aspect of course). There was much research put into this novel and if you have any interest on the subjects that Crichton tries to educate us on, you may be interested. <br /></span>

  <a href="/user/show/988178-wyatt" class="left imgcol" title="Wyatt"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1205373545p2/988178.jpg" alt="Wyatt" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/18139117?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 19, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/988178-wyatt" class="user" title="Wyatt">Wyatt</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7672.Congo" title="Paperback 9780060541835" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer18139117">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10071462983217321605">This was a great book,<br />but don't read under this or it will ruin the story for you. <br /><br /><br />This book takes place in many continents starting in the USA. First with an American team of ERTS who search for important geological parts of the earth for which they can extract important minerals or deposits. They have anonymous companies hire them to retrieve these resources that they need in neutral and allied countries. In this book Congo they are searching for type 11b Diamonds with a boron coating on them.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10071462983217321605">This was a great book,<br />but don't read under this or it will ruin the story for you. <br /><br /><br />This book takes place in many continents starting in the USA. First with an American team of ERTS who search for important geological parts of the earth for which they can extract important minerals or deposits. They have anonymous companies hire them to retrieve these resources that they need in neutral and allied countries. In this book Congo they are searching for type 11b Diamonds with a boron coating on them. This is important for making data transfer and computers run 100,000 times faster and hold just as much or more data then they had before. So this would put them 3 years ahead of other companies in those fields since all business's are competing, and you could make millions with a 3 week advance, then think about what you could do with a 3 year advance in technology that's well over billions of dollars. Well anyways, this ERTS sends a group of people to retrieve and find the diamonds in the Congo jungle in Africa. This team is doing well until they reach the mountain where the ruins of Zinj. The city that lost tales of Diamonds came from. So they've found what they are looking for. Then there camp is attacked by "Gorillas" who smash there heads with stones. Why stones? I'll explain later. Well the first team fails, so ERTS sends in another team. They get in contact with a Scientist named Elliot who has been training this Mountain Gorilla Amy sign language from a very young age. Smart Gorilla. Well this gorilla was brought back from Africa from an American tourist woman, since Amy's mom was killed by a crushed skull (the gorillas at Zinj did it). So they are all together the ERTS group, Elliot, Amy, and the Woman who entered MIT at 13. They all go to Tangeria if i remember right to pick up the person who's going to lead them safely through the Congo. They go through some hardships, espionage from opposing companies trying for this multi million dollar deal. Amy gets stolen, Civil war in Africa, Cannibalism in the Congo, midget tribes finding white men in jungle, automated machine guns shooting at attacking Gorillas, then Amy blowing up the Diamond mine and triggering the explosion of the Mountain to erupt on the Richter 9 scale. They get attacked by Cannibalistic tribes as they try to flee the erupting mountain. Then escape in a hot air balloon being fueled by many propane tanks from a plane crash meant to deliver supplies to the opposing country's searching for Diamonds. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10071462983217321605">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/19769273?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 08, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/973898-jason" class="user" title="Jason">Jason</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7672.Congo" title="Paperback 9780060541835" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer19769273">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18411135699139195661">would have given this book five stars but i've seen the movie which traumatized me with it's badness. although i literally finished the book in the parking lot of the theater the weekend it came out so it was very fresh in my mind and ready to be compared for all its shortcomings. was it fair to the movie? no. was it fair that they actually charged people to see that piece of *expletive deleted*? no. i say that makes us even. my problems with the book. not too many. it did what it wanted to do.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18411135699139195661">would have given this book five stars but i've seen the movie which traumatized me with it's badness. although i literally finished the book in the parking lot of the theater the weekend it came out so it was very fresh in my mind and ready to be compared for all its shortcomings. was it fair to the movie? no. was it fair that they actually charged people to see that piece of *expletive deleted*? no. i say that makes us even. my problems with the book. not too many. it did what it wanted to do. rambled a wee bit but most books do. my problems with the movie. oh where to start? how about the horrific casting. ernie hudson as monroe? the role could have been played perfectly by...tim curry! unfortunately mr. curry was playing a different role in the movie. one which he is used to playing: the villain. (see Legend, Rocky Horror, The Shadow, Kinsey and IT for reference). What makes this villain different from the others was that he wasn't necessary to the story. my proof of this accusation is that he wasn't even in the book. yes, you read that last sentence correctly. they made up a main villain for the movie. tim (im a huge fan and therefore reserve the right to refer to him by his first name) is an awesome actor playing a character that should never have existed. sad but true. other problems. monkeys look fake. you can almost see the zipper that opens the suit for the actors to get out them. monkeys are way dumber than they were in the book. what could have been an intense and frightening film was made into mindless action fluff. although the volcano eruption was cool. im too tired from bitching at the movie to keep going now. basically the book was WAY better than the movie and should be read if you like semi realistic horror/action. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18411135699139195661">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_534977508">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/534977508" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1197204-ruben" class="left imgcol" title="Ruben"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" alt="Ruben" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/534977508?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 13, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1197204-ruben" class="user" title="Ruben">Ruben</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7672.Congo" title="Paperback 9780060541835" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer534977508">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10845355531425903026">Congo wasn’t quite what I was expecting, but it seems to read like a typical Crichton book: Lots of detailed build-up; a climax that comes and goes faster than a Kardashian marriage/divorce; perfunctory wrap-up; acknowledgements. <br /><br />So far, the books I’ve read of Crichton’s get me excited with intriguing concepts and storylines, but then leave me feeling that he didn’t do as much as he could have with the “ingredients” he had in place. <br /><br />[spoiler alert…but do you really need the alert after this many</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10845355531425903026">Congo wasn’t quite what I was expecting, but it seems to read like a typical Crichton book: Lots of detailed build-up; a climax that comes and goes faster than a Kardashian marriage/divorce; perfunctory wrap-up; acknowledgements. <br /><br />So far, the books I’ve read of Crichton’s get me excited with intriguing concepts and storylines, but then leave me feeling that he didn’t do as much as he could have with the “ingredients” he had in place. <br /><br />[spoiler alert…but do you really need the alert after this many years?] <br /><br />For example, “killer gorillas that had a spoken language and were trained to kill.” For the love of Vishnu, Crichton created an army of killer talking apes that were going to kill a mercenary force and team of scientists! How cool is that?! <br /><br />Finally we meet the gorillas and they attack the humans and they are indeed overpowering the humans and about to annihilate them, and theeeeeen a volcano erupts and they all die. Acknowledgements. That’s the book. The main storyline wasn’t about the gorillas, but it might has well have been with all the buildup to them. <br /><br />It’d be like watching a Die Hard movie and right when Bruce Willis (John McClane) is about to make something huge explode, he decides, “You know…I should let the proper authorities handle this.” And then he dials 9-1-1, and theeeeeen Movie Credits. <br /><br />Or for you ladies, it’d be like watching a Ryan Gossling movie and right when he’s about to perform his ultimate romantic gesture to win over the female lead, he stops and says to himself, “Man, this chick is really high maintenance. Why, exactly, am I trying to win her over?” He goes back to his day job and theeeeeeen…Movie Credits. <br /><br />So, feel free to read Congo and just enjoy the ride but be prepared for a low payoff for your time. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10845355531425903026">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_48900089">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/48900089" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/30987-justine" class="left imgcol" title="Justine"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1186494631p2/30987.jpg" alt="Justine" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/48900089?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 11, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/30987-justine" class="user" title="Justine">Justine</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7672.Congo" title="Paperback 9780060541835" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer48900089">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9963545875224208223">Ah Congo. You are Joe's first Crichton (you never forget your first), and a god in the pantheon of semi-sciency adventures. Swashbuckling and debonair, you seamlessly blend "When Apes Attack" with "If I Could Talk With the Animals," and we are mightily entertained.<br /><br />Stuck in O'Hare (again, shocker), I bought me another Crichton book to wile away the hours. I think this may become something of a tradition, as Jurassic Park was purchased in the same terminal H bookstore and with the same raging weat</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9963545875224208223">Ah Congo. You are Joe's first Crichton (you never forget your first), and a god in the pantheon of semi-sciency adventures. Swashbuckling and debonair, you seamlessly blend "When Apes Attack" with "If I Could Talk With the Animals," and we are mightily entertained.<br /><br />Stuck in O'Hare (again, shocker), I bought me another Crichton book to wile away the hours. I think this may become something of a tradition, as Jurassic Park was purchased in the same terminal H bookstore and with the same raging weather outside. I digress. There is an odd feeling I get with these books which shows that once upon a time, I used to pay attention to what I read. In short: I remember-- snippets of feeling, insight, fear, excitement-- what I was feeling when I first read this as a young lass. Back then, this shit was profound (I was also in 5th grade.)<br /><br />Those of you who know me now, may know that I do not like simians. they are way too much like people, and since i generally don't like people... this fear may have been started by Congo's brain-smashing oar-wielding apes, and has been amply confirmed by the one in the zoo that caches rocks to throw at unsuspecting visitors and the famed Hannibal Lecter Xanax chimp (I kind of love him though). In short, monkeys are creepy. That's why this book is fantastic.<br /><br />For one, it reads REALLY fast. I can't remember the last time I picked up something that read this fast. Even Dahl doesn't. <br /><br />Beyond that, it's a fantastic relic of early 80s optimism and technological lust. Oh how gleefully he talks about computing. Oh how fantastic it all sounds with the Type II Boron coated diamonds. Oh how sexy that Karen Ross is-- with her math geniusness and expeditionary drive to find business information and money. Silly monkey man, how can you keep up?<br /><br />Also, middle of the jungle adventure (Crichton tries to inform the reader about some different issues in African history, but the effect is rather sallow-- but then again, it's hard to take a white man's introspection about the state of the Congo during a book about mineral rape and crazy-ass monkeys) is just awesome. I find myself wanting to take a trip. If only the Congo weren't a steaming, terrifying, pile of murder right now...<br /><br />This is a fucking classic. I will dream of crazy gorillas storming my encampment with verbal language and stone tools for several weeks. Fun. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9963545875224208223">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer64318408633830119">I would give 1/2 a star if I could. He gets that simply because he managed to get words on paper. I have never hated a book so much in my life. I thought it was ridiculous, had bad character development and a boring plot. I can't believe they even THOUGHT to make it a movie, but am not surprised that stunk as well.               <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1234190223">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7085210872888970007">Enjoyed this immensely! I have vague recollections of the movie, group goes to the Congo, take a communicating gorilla, bad gorillas attack, volcanic eruptions and Tim Curry haha but the book is so much better. I loved the amount of detail, the science parts, the historical parts and the 'atmosphere' that the author evoked of being in the Congo, brilliant!</span>

          </span>

  <a href="/user/show/16968146-benjamin-stahl" class="left imgcol" title="Benjamin Stahl"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1435493864p2/16968146.jpg" alt="Benjamin Stahl" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/871648906?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 12, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/16968146-benjamin-stahl" class="user" title="Benjamin Stahl">Benjamin Stahl</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7672.Congo" title="Paperback 9780060541835" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer871648906">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1994458937951450775"><strong>A <em>Heartbreak Hipster</em> Review</strong><br /><br /><em>Congo</em> is definitely the most boring and disappointing Crichton book I have read so far. <br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394832455i/8913357.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>That's right, nineties Dad. It was <em>boring</em>.</strong><br /><br />I had expected this one to be rather silly, but also <em>fun</em>. I haven't seen the movie, and I can't say I'm in any hurry to do so, either. The only thing I did know about this book, was that it involved a talking gorilla, a bunch of scientists, and an unknown species of hostile primates. <br /><br /><img width="200" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394832455i/8913358.jpg" /><img width="200" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394832455i/8913359.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>Fucking horrible creatures. But gorillas are okay.</strong><br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394832455i/8913360._SX540_.jpg" /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394832455i/8913361._SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br />Accordin</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1994458937951450775"><strong>A <em>Heartbreak Hipster</em> Review</strong><br /><br /><em>Congo</em> is definitely the most boring and disappointing Crichton book I have read so far. <br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394832455i/8913357.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>That's right, nineties Dad. It was <em>boring</em>.</strong><br /><br />I had expected this one to be rather silly, but also <em>fun</em>. I haven't seen the movie, and I can't say I'm in any hurry to do so, either. The only thing I did know about this book, was that it involved a talking gorilla, a bunch of scientists, and an unknown species of hostile primates. <br /><br /><img width="200" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394832455i/8913358.jpg" /><img width="200" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394832455i/8913359.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>Fucking horrible creatures. But gorillas are okay.</strong><br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394832455i/8913360._SX540_.jpg" /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394832455i/8913361._SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br />According to Dr Naan - one who is seemingly incapable of giving a straight fucking answer when he gets asked about his <em>UK Visa</em>, and yet can articulate like <em>Shakespeare</em> - when it comes to all his controversial scientific theories - some <strong>80%</strong> of females aged <strong>15 - 40</strong> are expected to have had at least <em>one</em> sexual dream, in which they get raped by three gorillas simultaneously. <br /><br /><img width="250" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394837428i/8914229.jpg" /><img width="150" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394837428i/8914230.png" /><br /><br /><strong>Now that <em>may</em> be so ... But it still does not justify what he and his cousins did to that poor little girl ...</strong> <br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394837428i/8914231._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br />Also ... according to my ex-girlfriend's brother ... some girls can be known to fantasize about <em>their</em> exes, getting their asses neatly handed to them by a steroid-fed mountain gorilla ... <em>just because they kept sending them messages on Facebook</em> ... <br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394837428i/8914232._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>Guy actually looks eerily similar to me ... like, maybe I should take this as an omen of some sort. Stop paying attention when my psychiatrist tells me that attending the High School reunion sounds a <em>great</em> fucking idea!!</strong><br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394837428i/8914233.jpg" /><br /><br />So that's my review of <em>Luke Neely</em>. He may have screwed a lot of things up, but deep down, I do believe he has a heart of gold, and all it takes is ... <strong>Oh ... Wait ...<br /><br />I'm supposed to be reviewing <em>Congo</em>, aren't I?</strong><br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394837428i/8914234._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br />Michael Crichton's <em>Congo</em> not only promises but <em>delivers</em> a trad-<br />itionally intriguing premise. After an American expedition, seek-<br />ing diamonds in the Congo jungle, gets murdered under strange circumstances, a rescue mission is sent in. These idiots enter the country under the political radar, because some kind of civil war is breaking out ... and indigenous tribes are attacking and killing the local population. <br />Karen Ross commands the ERTS Rescue Expedition. She calls in the help of an Ex-Mercenary named Munro. And, then, our true protagonists - Dr Elliot and his <em>Ameslan</em>-trained gorilla, "Amy" - make the joinings of the bandwagon from San Francisco.<br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394837428i/8914235.jpg" /><br /><br />Now listen here, people, because Mikey's not finished yet. <br />Little does Elliot know, that his cold-natured scientist friend has other intentions on her mind (she wants to locate, and excavate, the diamond-mines beneath some active volcano. <em>Oh, I thought we mentioned that on the brochure</em> ...<br />Whilst Doctor Elliot is determined to find the fabled Lost City of Zinj (spelt with a <em>silent</em> 'J', I assumed, because pronouncing it as "<em>Zinge</em>" just sounds gay.<br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395182261i/8962259._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>I didn't mean it like <em>that</em>, though ...</strong><br /><br />Anyway, this idea introduces various concepts; all of them shou- ld have been <em>awesome</em> in the hands of this talented author. <br />There was me, thinking there was gonna be outright gun-conflict between the Americans, and the Chinese; though it will probably sound lame, I had also wondered whether these strange <em>combat-trained</em> gorillas were eventually gonna team with the Americans, by using Amy as their translator. And <em>mostly</em>, I'd thought people were going to have their faces crushed by bloodthirsty primates - ( ... that is, when they weren't <em>already</em> being mauled by leopards, or getting swallowed by giant snakes). <br /><br /><strong>But what do we get instead?</strong> <br /><br /><img width="350" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395261683i/8973344.jpg" /><br /><br />"<em>RECVD MESG AURL INFO PLS EXPLN.<br />AXIDENTL DISKVRY VRY XCITNG-DISCRIMNT</em>".<br /><br /><strong>I'm sorry?</strong><br /><br />"<em>FUNXN COMPTRANLSS 99 CONFDNCE LIMITS TAPD.<br />AURL INFO (BRETHNG SOUNS) DEMNSTRTS</em>".<br /><br /><strong>Oh, I see ... wait, <em>what</em>?</strong> <br /><br />"<em>SOUND COMPLEX: ? AWAY - .5444 - .343.<br />SOUND COMPLEX: ? HERE - .6344 - .344</em>".<br /><br /><strong>Okay, so what you're saying is -</strong><br /><br />"<em>Amy(2) = distncton (£ + w%R), means <br />Grilla x 12 (&lt;.435 + !!!) reslt = .004</em>".<br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395263470i/8973490._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>Michael, I can't understand <em>any</em> of this shit!!!!<br /><br />What happened to the killer gorillas? <br /><br />What happened to that ancient city?<br /><br />What just happened to my <em>brain</em>?</strong><br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395263470i/8973491.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>If <em>you</em> had been my Science teacher in high school, then I probably <em>would've</em> had the guts to jump off the music-room balcony in front of my friends.</strong> <br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395266385i/8973764.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>"Hey Idiot!!! Put down that guitar and get your ass back on drums!!! Where are you, Fuckstain!! Douchebag, we need to <em>practise</em>!!! Fuckstai - <br /><em>Ohhh ... Oh, what a mess".</em></strong><br /><br />Now of <em>course</em> I understand that this is what all fans expect from Mr. Crichton. But sometimes it <em>does</em> get a little over the top. And I can't imagine <em>anyone</em> actually taking the time to decipher what this guy is really saying. I am not asking him to dumb it down ... <em>because unfortunately, that's no longer possbile</em> ... <br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395263470i/8973492._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>And I don't want him to write like a brainless idiot ...</strong> <br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395267154i/8973984.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>"Monkey make booboo on Man's face. "Ouchy!!!!!" Man scream. "I tink my nose is broked, and my eye hang like tail". Man run around in circle. Monkey twist his head".</strong><br /><br />But really I would have appreciated him putting just a <em>little</em> more thought into whether or not all his scientific expo was backed up with the thriller elements that most fans also tend to expect from him. Even in his last novel - <em>Micro</em> - which was terribly written, I still gave it <strong>3 Stars</strong>, because it had a good and entertaining body count. Kudos to Michael for not just resorting to cheap, mindless action scenes, but <em>my God</em>, was this story a boring one to read!!!<br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395313059i/8978434._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>Does <em>this</em> look boring? Hell <em>no</em>, it doesn't!!</strong><br /><br />But the book has barely anything to be frightened of. I mean, he did introduce the <em>threat</em> of the cannibals earlier on. And he does go into the extensive causalities suffered by such other explorers that tried to navigate through the Congo in their time. <br />But the people in this story just breeze through the jungle, as if it were their own backyard, fiddling with their high-tech gadgetry, and setting up camp whenever they get tired. <br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380394209r/758982._SX540_SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br />There is some cutesy charm in having a communicative gorilla. And I am surprised to say that the characters here were probably the most real that I have ever read of Crichton. But that is not to say that they were <em>good</em>. Only that, for the first time ever, he has allowed his characters to show at least some human emotions in the face of imminent death. Ross actually <em>cries</em> when she realizes that the computer terminal back in Houston won't save her from the Congo Army's missiles. While Munro feels mostly like a poor man's Quint (you know, that other caricature from <em>Jaws</em>) - I still liked the fact that he willingly stopped thinking about those silly diamonds ... and started acting like he genuinely cared about his life, and the lives of the others. <br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395345467i/8982838.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>Do you love <em>this</em> town, asshole?</strong><br /><br />So yeah, I'm not going to take the usual path with this writer and complain about his cardboard characters. These ones were more like <em>plastic</em>. If they were storage boxes, they'd look pretty boring, but at least they get the job done. Plus there is much less chance of them breaking through at the underside - when you are trying to sneak your pornography mags into the attic - and they spill all over the landing, and one goes down the gap in the stairs, and no matter what you do, you just can't get it out, and eventually your mother comes along and is like, "Hey! Something's been wedged between the stairs. Don't worry, son - run along now. Your mum won't rest till she finds a way to get it back. Run along now - and I'll get your homework back for you. Sweet, most innocent, pure-minded child that you are. Don't you be sweating so - I will soon have it in my hands, sweet Catholic-raised " etc etc etc ... <br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395359080i/8985468.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>This is a <em>Gongo</em>. It rhymes with <em>Congo</em>, you see.</strong><br /><br />Now, for God's sake, I told myself last time around, that I would cool it with these freaking reviews. I am putting more effort into <em>these</em> than I am with my <em>proper</em> writing. <br /><em>Umm</em> ... <em>okay</em> ... so while there was nothing really <em>bad</em> about this book, I had been planning to give it a <strong>2 Star</strong> rating right up until the end. The writing was pretty good. And most of the characters were surprisingly not terrible. Only there was just so much more potential, and Crichton did not so much <em>fail</em> to see that, as much as <em>know</em> it was there and simply not bother.<br /><em>Some</em> people died ... <em>eventually</em> ... except their deaths were never actually <em>seen</em>. We're just told afterwards, that some guy we didn't know the name of was found dead outside the campsite. It's kind of hard giving a shit about any of this. <br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395359080i/8985469.jpg" /><br /><br /><em>Nobody important dies</em>!! And even the few deaths that <em>did</em> occur just ended up feeling so <em>unsatisfying</em>. I don't mean to sound like a Tarantino fan, though; by "unsatisfying", I only mean that they didn't have any effect on the other characters whatsoever ... thus there was never any <em>tension</em> or <em>threat</em> established. <br /><br />(<em>Oh yeah - that just reminded me!! Crichton also took a leaf out of Stephen King's book, and fucking kept reminding the reader, throughout the story, that all the protagonists DO survive!! <br />For some reason, he uses that device where the characters keep on commenting on everything that is happening - (during some sort of interview, after the events of the novel) - just so you can rest assured that your favourite characters are not going to die. Now this wouldn't have been so irritating ... had there actually been a purpose for it. But honestly it serves nothing. There was no reason why we had to get the their retrospective thoughts as opposed to their initial reactions</em>).<br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395359080i/8985470._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>(ShUdDeRs In ReVuLsIoN ... )</strong><br /><br />The idea that they are trapped in the middle of the jungle, with a diminishing supply of ammunition, and the apes bound to attack them every night till they all get killed; <em>that</em> idea could and really <em>should</em> have worked. <br />There was one part, in particular - my favourite part of the entire book - where they try to get back out of the jungle. While they do not ever <em>see</em> the gorillas during this deserate act - they eventually hear something coming from within the enveloping foliage .... <em>an eerie orchestra of gentle sighing</em>; the sound the apes make when they are watching - and just hearing <em>this</em> is enough to creep them out and drive them back to their camp again. <br /><em>That</em> was really clever, because not only did it establish that they truly <em>are</em> trapped in their situation - but it also provided a subtle, though quite creepy, characteristic to the enemy. <br />Except there was one thing Mr. Medical Degree never stopped to realize. Once I'd thought about it, I felt like real hot shit, and was crossing my fingers that it wouldn't occur to him at all. <br /><br /><strong>Would you like to hear it?</strong><br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395359080i/8985471.jpg" /><br /><br />So these guys are surrounded by a dangerous jungle. <br />Out of this jungle comes a marauding army of deadly gorillas. <br />And to top that all off, the ammunition and defence equipment's steadily running out. Too many sides to cover ... and not enough supplies to keep it up. <strong>Am I correct?</strong> <br />Fucking sure as I'm gonna die a worthless piece of shit, I am. <br />So all this worrying brings me to question the most obvious flaw in your set-up, Mr. Crichton. Like, half a mile away, there lies an empty city. Now, forgive me, if I've let my imagination get ahead of me, but <em>surely</em>, these guys would be better off taking their shit into one small building, one small room, of said abandoned city. That way they only have one doorway to guard, as opposed to an encircling jungle. <br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395359080i/8985472.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>You go ahead and call me <em>pompous</em>, ma'am. But I know who I would rather go into the Congo with.</strong><br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395529495i/9010336._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>Benjamin:</strong> "The village should be just over that mountain". <br /><strong>Elliot:</strong> "Thank God. I'm sick of this jungle".<br /><strong>Michael:</strong> "Hey guys, have you seen these flowers?"<br /><strong>Benjamin:</strong> "Yeah, Mike, they're nice. But now's not the time - "<br /><strong>Michael:</strong> "<em>Nice</em>. These not just <em>nice</em>".<br /><strong>Elliot:</strong> Oh God, I think I just saw a gorilla behind that tree".<br /><strong>Michael:</strong> "I believe the correct term, Doctor, is <em>Beringei</em>".<br /><strong>Elliot:</strong> "Is that their scientific name or something?"<br /><strong>Benjamin:</strong> "Okay, guys, who gives a shit - Where is it? <em>OHHH GAAHD</em>!!!!"<br /><strong>Elliot:</strong> "Oh Jesus!! The gorilla's got him!!"<br /><strong>Michael:</strong> "Indeed ... umm ... <em>gosh</em>!!!"<br /><strong>Benjamin:</strong> (LOSES HIS ARM/SCREAMS INCOHERENTLY!!!)<br /><strong>Elliot:</strong> "What should we do? Should we help him?<br /><strong>Michael:</strong> "Ah, now ... you can't mess with nature"<br /><strong>Elliot:</strong> "Yes, but - "<br /><strong>Benjamin:</strong> (RIBCAGE NOW CRUSHED/GURGLING ON HIS OWN BLOOD!!!)<br /><strong>Michael:</strong> "Just watch how it kills. It's amazing".<br /><br /><img width="400" height="250" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395522814i/9009843.png" /><br /><br /><strong>I've always heard that he was a prick in real life.</strong><br /><br />Anyway, so I can wrap this up, and post it on Facebook - (further establishing how fucking pathetic I am) - let me give my opinion of this book in a nutshell. <br /><em>Congo</em> was overall a very disappointing book. Certainly not one I would recommend, if you are reading Crichton for the first time. Some parts were kinda cool - but for all these, there were always two parts more that just failed to hit the target one expects when reading something by this <em>usually satisfying</em> author. <br /><br /><strong>So there we go. I really don't think all this other bullshit I wrote was necessary at all. I'm sorry :(<br /><br />More bullshit reviews here: <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/370524-heartbreak-hipster---book-reviews?chapter=1" target="_blank">https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/...</a></strong><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1994458937951450775">...more</a>
