<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_581592498">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/581592498" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2898408-greg-cummings" class="left imgcol" title="Greg Cummings"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1405358766p2/2898408.jpg" alt="Greg Cummings" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/581592498?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 04, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2898408-greg-cummings" class="user" title="Greg Cummings">Greg Cummings</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7672.Congo" title="Paperback 9780060541835" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2898408-greg-cummings?shelf=gorillaland" class="actionLinkLite">gorillaland</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer581592498">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13498999546838431628">Although the scenario is somewhat naive - an unknown mutant subspecies of gorilla has for generations defended a lucrative diamond mine in the heart of the Congo jungle - this book played a big part in my career in gorilla conservation. In it Crichton describes the use of satellite data to prospect for the Lost City of Zinj in the central African jungles. With uncanny synchronicity, at the same time as I was reading about it, NASA was imaging the gorilla habitat in central Africa using radar onb</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13498999546838431628">Although the scenario is somewhat naive - an unknown mutant subspecies of gorilla has for generations defended a lucrative diamond mine in the heart of the Congo jungle - this book played a big part in my career in gorilla conservation. In it Crichton describes the use of satellite data to prospect for the Lost City of Zinj in the central African jungles. With uncanny synchronicity, at the same time as I was reading about it, NASA was imaging the gorilla habitat in central Africa using radar onboard the space shuttle Endeavour. My friend Peter Elliot, an ape actor, informed me Hollywood was planning to turn it into a movie. I contacted director Sam Mercer and offered him the radar image for a $10,000 donation to the gorillas (neglecting to mention that NASA-owned content is public property). Subsequently, I played a part in Paramount Picture's making of the movie in Hollywood, an experience that's given me heaps of material for my own writing. <br /><br />Despite the involvement of Kathleen Marshall who produced Jurassic Park, Michael Crichton distanced himself from the motion picture, saying, 'They're making a movie of my book. So what?' Critics mercilessly panned CONGO, but the book sparked something in me, inspiring some of the themes in my own writing. <br /><br />A worthy romp from a master of original plots.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13498999546838431628">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_62837230">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62837230" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2506057-sarai" class="left imgcol" title="Sarai"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1295027741p2/2506057.jpg" alt="Sarai" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/62837230?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 09, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2506057-sarai" class="user" title="Sarai">Sarai</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7672.Congo" title="Paperback 9780060541835" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2506057-sarai?shelf=general-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">general-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer62837230">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14151296518884977824">Kirkus Review: Entertainer-educator Crichton, that clever devil, has done it again - by dressing up one of the oldest book/movie scenarios around with enough capsulized science, history, and geography to keep readers happily on their toes. It's an expedition to darkest Africa, to the northeast corner of the Congo rain forest in Zaire, in search of a lost city (Zinj) full of diamonds and danger. Old hat, right? Wrong. Because this expedition, led by Karen Ross of Earth Resources Technology Servic</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14151296518884977824">Kirkus Review: Entertainer-educator Crichton, that clever devil, has done it again - by dressing up one of the oldest book/movie scenarios around with enough capsulized science, history, and geography to keep readers happily on their toes. It's an expedition to darkest Africa, to the northeast corner of the Congo rain forest in Zaire, in search of a lost city (Zinj) full of diamonds and danger. Old hat, right? Wrong. Because this expedition, led by Karen Ross of Earth Resources Technology Services (ERTS) in Houston, is the nth degree in hi-tech - portable computers, laser-beam navigation, satellite TV-hookup with Houston - and the juxtaposition of super-gadgetry with nature at its wildest is simply splendid. Furthermore, since a previous ERTS trek to Zinj was decimated by gorilla-like creatures (according to videotape analysis), primate expert Peter Elliot is along; and with him is adorable gorilla Amy - who understands English and is fluent in sign language. (By coincidence, Amy's been having nightmares about a city that looks just like legendary Zinj.) So there's lively lecture material a-plenty - computers, zoology, linguistics, Congo botany, etc. - as Karen, Peter, Amy, and mercenary Munro (what used to be the Robert Shaw role) head towards Zinj via parachute jump, river-rapids, and mountain-climbing. . . while fending off cannibals, an angry hippo, guided missiles, and sophisticated sabotage by a rival German-Japanese team. (The Zinj diamonds are the raw material for computer-chips that will revolutionize everything.) And when they do arrive at Zinj, where the rival team has been massacred, the ERTS team is soon under attack by this odd mutant killer-gorilla species - descendants of apes who were long ago trained to be ruthless guards of the diamond hoard.<br /><br />If you saw the movie Congo, it's nothign like this book. Congo the movie ranks among the worst movies I've ever seen, which was sooooooooo disappointing because I really enjoyed this book and because it had Tim Curry in it (who is one of my favorite actors). Congo the movie SUCKED. Congo the book rocks. As with other Michael Crichton fare, it's a thick book and packed with true information mixed with the fiction so you're never sure if you're reading something that actually happened or not. I would definitely recommend this to anyone who has read another Crichton novel and liked it.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14151296518884977824">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_631591017">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/631591017" itemprop="url" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/631591017?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 03, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8044108-ingrid-espinosa" class="user" title="Ingrid Espinosa">Ingrid Espinosa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7672.Congo" title="Paperback 9780060541835" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer631591017">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1898968950128897005">I hadn't been reading within my favorite genres for a while, and this was a welcome return.<br /><br />As always, Crichton leaves you hanging a every chapter, and I couldn't help but read Congo in just a few sittings (if i read it in one, would it count as a short story?). The threat of the gorillas breathing genuinely kept me on my guard from the beginning.<br /><br />My critique though, is that I thought the resolution of the killer gorilla mystery was a little unimpressive - i was getting my mind prepared for some r</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1898968950128897005">I hadn't been reading within my favorite genres for a while, and this was a welcome return.<br /><br />As always, Crichton leaves you hanging a every chapter, and I couldn't help but read Congo in just a few sittings (if i read it in one, would it count as a short story?). The threat of the gorillas breathing genuinely kept me on my guard from the beginning.<br /><br />My critique though, is that I thought the resolution of the killer gorilla mystery was a little unimpressive - i was getting my mind prepared for some real weird not-gorilla not-man predator, particularly with the emphasis they had put on that and the oddness of their manner of killing. similar was their escape thanks to nature (though it wasn't easy, fine). I had also expected some more development in Ross character...but Munro was entertaining enough (although I expected him to be more sinister...nonetheless he was pretty likeable, as were the porters). <br /><br />Nevertheless I was very happy with Congo. Fast-paced, intelligent fun, with a real warning to boot. <br />I'll always be a fan of Crichton's style, and that was more than enough to reel me in on this adventure.<br /><br />3.25/5</span>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1190402647">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1190402647" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/16294266-madhulika-liddle" class="left imgcol" title="Madhulika Liddle"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1444124482p2/16294266.jpg" alt="Madhulika Liddle" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1190402647?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 04, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/16294266-madhulika-liddle" class="user" title="Madhulika Liddle">Madhulika Liddle</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7672.Congo" title="Paperback 9780060541835" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1190402647">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4794609930958996356">In June 1979, a party of geologists searching for industrial blue diamonds in Congo's dense jungles of the Virunga area is savagely attacked and wiped out by <em>something</em>. Back at headquarters in Houston, geologist, geek and sometime child prodigy Dr Karen Ross insists on setting off on another expedition, to get to the diamonds <em>and</em> discover what happened to her colleagues. This results in her approaching a primatologist named Dr Peter Elliott, who has spent several years teaching sign language to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4794609930958996356">In June 1979, a party of geologists searching for industrial blue diamonds in Congo's dense jungles of the Virunga area is savagely attacked and wiped out by <em>something</em>. Back at headquarters in Houston, geologist, geek and sometime child prodigy Dr Karen Ross insists on setting off on another expedition, to get to the diamonds <em>and</em> discover what happened to her colleagues. This results in her approaching a primatologist named Dr Peter Elliott, who has spent several years teaching sign language to a gorilla named Amy. Amy's recent nightmares have prompted her to start painting distinctive ruins in jungles, and Peter is convinced the answer to Amy's distress lies in the Congo, from where she was brought as an infant. <br /><br />So Ross, Elliott, and Amy go off to the rain forests of Congo, guided by a mercenary named Munro. Simultaneously, civil war breaks out; this part of Africa begins to seethe, and the cannibalistic Kigani go on the rampage. As if that wasn't enough, the volcano our protagonists are headed towards has begun to get restless... <em>and</em> there is that ominous presence, somewhere in the jungles around them, which ferociously guards the mythical lost City of Zinj, home to legendary riches. <br /><br />I was underwhelmed by <em>Congo</em>. This is the sort of adventure that might've worked a hundred years ago, when Africa was still regarded as the Dark Continent, a forbidding, dangerous place: the setting for the Tarzan series, or <em>King Solomon's Mines</em>. In this day and age, the style and content—cramming the adventure with just about everything <em>exotic</em> and <em>wild</em> about Africa—makes the story just a little too <em>fantastic</em>. It's almost as if Crichton sat down and listed everything he'd ever seen or heard about regarding Africa, past and present, and then bunged it in here. The ruins of a fabled city of enormous wealth (an African El Dorado, so to say)? Check. Vicious creatures that smash people's heads and vanish into the night? Check. Hippos attacking boats on rivers? Check. Volcanoes? Check. Cannibals? Pygmies? Civil war? Erupting volcanoes? Check, check, <em>check</em>. <br /><br />Along the way there are some interesting insights into everything from military technology to the behaviour of apes, but these occasionally end up coming in the way of the story itself, the story being put on hold while we're told how World War III will be fought and in how much time, etc, etc. For me, another major irritant was the fact that every now and then the narrative changed slightly to go into past perfect: <em>"—was to later say that..."</em>, which of course gives away the fact that X survived this hair-raising ordeal. <br /><br />Not terrible, but certainly not one of Crichton's better books. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4794609930958996356">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/729387-caprice-hokstad" class="left imgcol" title="Caprice Hokstad"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1411962829p2/729387.jpg" alt="Caprice Hokstad" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1409605137?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 05, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/729387-caprice-hokstad" class="user" title="Caprice Hokstad">Caprice Hokstad</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7672.Congo" title="Paperback 9780060541835" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1409605137">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1680689662649336945">I give it a 2.5, which rounds to a 3, but I only barely liked it more than Prey. I was annoyed by the omniscient narration, but my hyper-sensitivity to that is probably related to being a writer. I also had a bit of a hard time finding a protag to root for besides Amy, the signing gorilla who was hauled on a trip to her homeland for nebulous reasons having very little to do with her. Her human companion Elliot was likeable enough, but he had almost no means of moving the plot and was basically d</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1680689662649336945">I give it a 2.5, which rounds to a 3, but I only barely liked it more than Prey. I was annoyed by the omniscient narration, but my hyper-sensitivity to that is probably related to being a writer. I also had a bit of a hard time finding a protag to root for besides Amy, the signing gorilla who was hauled on a trip to her homeland for nebulous reasons having very little to do with her. Her human companion Elliot was likeable enough, but he had almost no means of moving the plot and was basically dragged along most of the time.<br /><br />The main mover of plot was a women utterly obsessed with finding diamonds at any cost and her obsession cost more than a few lives, but not hers. I could not find any good qualities to offset her negative ones and felt like she was almost a token "bitch" character.<br /><br />The climax was a bit anti-climactic, and the aftermath of the failed expedition was rather depressing in just about all areas. A major scientific discovery wasn't even reported because of loss of proof, but there had been transmissions sent that should have been recorded on the other end and safe from the catastrophe that hit the expedition.<br /><br />Would not read again. Still plan to read Jurassic Park when the library waitlist gives me my turn.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1308070361">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1308070361" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/33198239-niah" class="left imgcol" title="Niah"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1447956786p2/33198239.jpg" alt="Niah" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1308070361?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 19, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/33198239-niah" class="user" title="Niah">Niah</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7672.Congo" title="Paperback 9780060541835" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/33198239-niah?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1308070361">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17600374988944698020">I do not say this lightly: Michael Crichton is brilliant. This novel is brilliant. (For those who don’t know, Crichton is the author of <em>Jurassic Park</em> among other works).<br /><br />The beginning of this book is <strong>slow</strong>. So much so that I didn’t think I would like the rest of the book. Boy, was I wrong. Crichton’s prologue was so intense and ended in so much suspense that I believed it could get better. At times he packs in overly-technical writing. These were the times it got lengthy. Frankly, I don’t care muc</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17600374988944698020">I do not say this lightly: Michael Crichton is brilliant. This novel is brilliant. (For those who don’t know, Crichton is the author of <em>Jurassic Park</em> among other works).<br /><br />The beginning of this book is <strong>slow</strong>. So much so that I didn’t think I would like the rest of the book. Boy, was I wrong. Crichton’s prologue was so intense and ended in so much suspense that I believed it could get better. At times he packs in overly-technical writing. These were the times it got lengthy. Frankly, I don’t care much about the technical aspect. I don’t know if it’s true or not. Still, the technical part lessens around day 3 and the book got <strong>really good</strong>. <br /><br />This book was at times thrilling, and although it is fiction, there are a lot of interesting facts. For instance, did you know that some chimpanzees eat human infants in the wild? I personally did not. Of course I knew that you could teach apes to sign (cough <em>Planet of the Apes</em> cough) but this made me consider just how remarkable that is. I never would have considered just how brilliant primates are before reading this. <br /><br />The characters aren’t terrible. Not the most remarkable but that’s alright. Amy (the gorilla) was my favorite. Especially when she tears up a drawing that symbolizes her tearing up a woman (Crichton had me chuckling a few times, I admit). <br /><br />If you’re a fan of the <em>Planet of the Apes</em> franchise (new or old) or enjoyed <em>Jurassic Park</em>, I think this is definitely something you will enjoy. Also, if you recently saw the Monster Week documentary of<em> Cannibal in the Jungle</em>, this was similar in many ways. I’m still rather mind blown. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17600374988944698020">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1285281675?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 20, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/30116089-dark-inferno" class="user" title="Dark Inferno">Dark Inferno</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/847995.Congo" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780099544319" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1285281675">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7072278090872808202">I bought this book for two reasons:<br /><br />1 - I love the Movie<br /><br />2 - It was on sale for 1 at Asda, and after reading it I'm glad i got it on offer.<br /><br />This was not a disappointing read, I read it in less than a fortnight and found it relativly satisfying. However, I'd say this is one one of those rare books whichinspired a movie that is just about supperior in every way, the primeape version of jaws movie and book comparison if you will. If i had never seen the movie i may have have given it 5 stars. <br /><br />As i was</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7072278090872808202">I bought this book for two reasons:<br /><br />1 - I love the Movie<br /><br />2 - It was on sale for £1 at Asda, and after reading it I'm glad i got it on offer.<br /><br />This was not a disappointing read, I read it in less than a fortnight and found it relativly satisfying. However, I'd say this is one one of those rare books whichinspired a movie that is just about supperior in every way, the primeape version of jaws movie and book comparison if you will. If i had never seen the movie i may have have given it 5 stars. <br /><br />As i was reading it I seemed to get the impression it was written to a scedule, and Crichton had a mimmum word limit. There was so much detail into the relativly in consiquential to try and explain key moments, it felt almost suffocating. There is also so much tecnical information and explanation provided, yet without a layman's term's summary, i was almost ready to place it back on the self and not look back. <br /><br />The book is constantly switiching tenses,describing what the character is doing and then, in the next paragraph, informing you about something he did after the events of the book; something i found not only very annoying but which also saped much of the tension in the proccess. <br /><br />In my opinion, this book is ok, certainly could have been better but well worth a read if you come upon it on offer. Though I would say, spend the extra and buy the movie. Or if you really want to try a Michael Crichton Noveel, bypass Congo and go straight for Jurasic Park.</span>

      <a href="/user/show/47081-mark-r" class="user" title="Mark R.">Mark R.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7672.Congo" title="Paperback 9780060541835" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1335978235">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10621535495999295466">A privately funded expedition heads to the Congo in search of valuable blue diamonds. The diamonds are located in a legendary lost city, which recent reports suggest is not simply a myth, as previously believed. Along for the ride is a gorilla trained in sign language, whose recent finger paintings closely resemble the reported lost city.<br /><br />With that setup, “Congo” isn’t as thrilling as it should be. Michael Crichton mixes plenty of science fact in with his science fiction, but the blend of the two</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10621535495999295466">A privately funded expedition heads to the Congo in search of valuable blue diamonds. The diamonds are located in a legendary lost city, which recent reports suggest is not simply a myth, as previously believed. Along for the ride is a gorilla trained in sign language, whose recent finger paintings closely resemble the reported lost city.<br /><br />With that setup, “Congo” isn’t as thrilling as it should be. Michael Crichton mixes plenty of science fact in with his science fiction, but the blend of the two isn’t as seamless as in some of his other books. Frequently a character will reference a device or piece of technology, and the following paragraphs then bring the reader up to speed on the uses and history of said device.<br /><br />There’s a lot to peak a reader’s interest (I know I was intrigued by the fact of sign-language-using gorillas), but ultimately the action falls a little flat, and could be more detailed. The human characters are fine, but the gorilla, Amy, is perhaps more interesting than the remainder of the group.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10621535495999295466">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Come to think of it, if you're also interested in the future of data transfer speed and diamonds, this is definitely for you.<br />The big star in this story is Amy, a gorilla with a 620 sign vocabulary. After reading this, you will want a gorilla for a best friend.</span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1360215788" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/199853-andre-dumas" class="left imgcol" title="Andre Dumas"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1355094529p2/199853.jpg" alt="Andre Dumas" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1360215788?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 17, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/199853-andre-dumas" class="user" title="Andre Dumas">Andre Dumas</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7672.Congo" title="Paperback 9780060541835" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1360215788">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3158958902216632842">I always admire Michael Crichton for the in your face shocking moments. In Jurassic Park, it's when the nurse opens the door to find a dinosaur gnawing off a baby's face. And in Congo, it's when the guy thinks Tree Monkey's are throwing berries at him when in fact it's a HUMAN EYEBALL. Those kinds of things really make these novels thrive. However, I found that after that moment, Congo kind of flat-lined on the monitor for me. I was expecting way more crazy Gorilla action here, but surprisingly,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3158958902216632842">I always admire Michael Crichton for the in your face shocking moments. In Jurassic Park, it's when the nurse opens the door to find a dinosaur gnawing off a baby's face. And in Congo, it's when the guy thinks Tree Monkey's are throwing berries at him when in fact it's a HUMAN EYEBALL. Those kinds of things really make these novels thrive. However, I found that after that moment, Congo kind of flat-lined on the monitor for me. I was expecting way more crazy Gorilla action here, but surprisingly, the Gorilla action doesn't actually come until about 85% of the way through. There was a lot of technical talk regarding diamonds, and volcanoes and sunspots that I just didn't seem to care about. All I want is more murderous Gorilla's. Is that too much to ask? </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3158958902216632842">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ImqgyzjXEzRPOfnpvjuqJcIfak0srv6x2qGkyIU5rSZHvp8YygUHzsPhjVLAWkyXi+ipVGVzuRuwqKFaSaxbYw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton">About Michael Crichton</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton"><img alt="5194" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1359042651p2/5194.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer1554661779825752500">Michael Crichton (1942–2008) was one of the most successful novelists of his generation, admired for his meticulous scientific research and fast-paced narrative. He graduated summa cum laude and earned his MD from Harvard Medical School in 1969. His first novel, <a title="Odds On" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18078737.Odds_On">Odds On</a> (1966), was written under the pseudonym <a title="John Lange" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12619.John_Lange">John Lange</a> and was followed by seven more Lange novels. He also wrote as <a title="Michael Douglas" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/85503.Michael_Douglas">Michael Douglas</a></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1554661779825752500">Michael Crichton (1942–2008) was one of the most successful novelists of his generation, admired for his meticulous scientific research and fast-paced narrative. He graduated summa cum laude and earned his MD from Harvard Medical School in 1969. His first novel, <a title="Odds On" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18078737.Odds_On">Odds On</a> (1966), was written under the pseudonym <a title="John Lange" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12619.John_Lange">John Lange</a> and was followed by seven more Lange novels. He also wrote as <a title="Michael Douglas" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/85503.Michael_Douglas">Michael Douglas</a> and <a title="Jeffery Hudson" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/607284.Jeffery_Hudson">Jeffery Hudson</a>. His novel <a title="A Case of Need" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=A%20Case%20of%20Need">A Case of Need</a> won the Edgar Award in 1969. Popular throughout the world, he has sold more than 200 million books. His novels have been translated into thirty-eight languages, and thirteen have been made into films.<br /><br />Michael Crichton passed away from lymphoma in 2008. He was 66 years old.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1554661779825752500">...more</a>

    </div>
